RSA</a></li><!--]--><!--[--><li class="item sub-chapter" data-v-2c51c6a5><a class="link sub-chapter-title" href="/en/documentation/red_hat_enterprise_linux/6/html/security_guide/sect-dsa" id="sub-link-to-sect-DSA" data-v-2c51c6a5>A.2.3. DSA</a></li><!--]--><!--[--><li class="item sub-chapter" data-v-2c51c6a5><a class="link sub-chapter-title" href="/en/documentation/red_hat_enterprise_linux/6/html/security_guide/sect-ssl_tls" id="sub-link-to-sect-SSL_TLS" data-v-2c51c6a5>A.2.4. SSL/TLS</a></li><!--]--><!--[--><li class="item sub-chapter" data-v-2c51c6a5><a class="link sub-chapter-title" href="/en/documentation/red_hat_enterprise_linux/6/html/security_guide/sect-cramer-shoup_cryptosystem" id="sub-link-to-sect-Cramer-Shoup_Cryptosystem" data-v-2c51c6a5>A.2.5. Cramer-Shoup Cryptosystem</a></li><!--]--><!--[--><li class="item sub-chapter" data-v-2c51c6a5><a class="link sub-chapter-title" href="/en/documentation/red_hat_enterprise_linux/6/html/security_guide/sect-elgamal-encryption" id="sub-link-to-sect-ElGamal-Encryption" data-v-2c51c6a5>A.2.6. ElGamal Encryption</a></li><!--]--><!--]--></ol></details></li><!--]--><!--]--></ol></details></li><li class="item chapter" data-v-28afad38><details id="toc--app-Audit_Reference" data-v-28afad38><summary class="heading chapter-title" id="app-Audit_Reference--summary" data-v-28afad38>B. Audit System Reference</summary><ol class="sub-nav" data-v-28afad38><li class="item sub-chapter" data-v-28afad38><a class="link sub-chapter-title chapter-landing-page" href="/en/documentation/red_hat_enterprise_linux/6/html/security_guide/app-audit_reference" id="chapter-landing--app-Audit_Reference" data-v-28afad38>Audit System Reference</a></li><!--[--><!--[--><li class="item sub-chapter" data-v-2c51c6a5><a class="link sub-chapter-title" href="/en/documentation/red_hat_enterprise_linux/6/html/security_guide/app-audit_reference#sec-Audit_Events_Fields" id="sub-link-to-sec-Audit_Events_Fields" data-v-2c51c6a5>B.1. Audit Event Fields</a></li><!--]--><!--[--><li class="item sub-chapter" data-v-2c51c6a5><a class="link sub-chapter-title" href="/en/documentation/red_hat_enterprise_linux/6/html/security_guide/sec-audit_record_types" id="sub-link-to-sec-Audit_Record_Types" data-v-2c51c6a5>B.2. Audit Record Types</a></li><!--]--><!--]--></ol></details></li><li class="item chapter" data-v-28afad38><a class="link" href="/en/documentation/red_hat_enterprise_linux/6/html/security_guide/appe-security_guide-revision_history" id="chapter-landing--appe-Security_Guide-Revision_History" data-v-28afad38>C. Revision History</a></li><li class="item chapter" data-v-28afad38><a class="link" href="/en/documentation/red_hat_enterprise_linux/6/html/security_guide/legal-notice" id="chapter-landing--idm139870065614832" data-v-28afad38>Legal Notice</a></li><!--]--></ol></nav><!----></div></aside><article class="content span-xs-12 span-sm-6 span-md-12 span-lg-7" aria-live="polite" data-v-62e1e993><!----><div lang="en-us" xml:lang="en-us" class="docs-content-container" data-v-62e1e993><!----><h1 data-id="content_chapter" class="chapter-title" data-v-62e1e993>Chapter 7. System Auditing</h1><div id="pdf-download" data-v-62e1e993><pf-icon icon="download" data-v-62e1e993><span class="sr-only" data-v-62e1e993>download</span></pf-icon><a href="/en-us/documentation/red_hat_enterprise_linux/6/pdf/security_guide/Red_Hat_Enterprise_Linux-6-Security_Guide-en-US.pdf" data-v-62e1e993> PDF </a><hr data-v-62e1e993></div><section class="rhdocs" data-v-62e1e993><body><div xml:lang="en-US" class="chapter" id="chap-system_auditing" lang="en-US"><div class="para">
		The Linux Audit system provides a way to track security-relevant information on your system. Based on pre-configured rules, Audit generates log entries to record as much information about the events that are happening on your system as possible. This information is crucial for mission-critical environments to determine the violator of the security policy and the actions they performed. Audit does not provide additional security to your system; rather, it can be used to discover violations of security policies used on your system. These violations can further be prevented by additional security measures such as SELinux.
	</div><div class="para">
		The following list summarizes some of the information that Audit is capable of recording in its log files:
	</div><div class="itemizedlist"><ul><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Date and time, type, and outcome of an event.
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Sensitivity labels of subjects and objects.
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Association of an event with the identity of the user who triggered the event.
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				All modifications to Audit configuration and attempts to access Audit log files.
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				All uses of authentication mechanisms, such as SSH, Kerberos, and others.
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Changes to any trusted database, such as <code class="filename">/etc/passwd</code>.
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Attempts to import or export information into or from the system.
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Include or exclude events based on user identity, subject and object labels, and other attributes.
			</div></li></ul></div><div class="para">
		The use of the Audit system is also a requirement for a number of security-related certifications. Audit is designed to meet or exceed the requirements of the following certifications or compliance guides:
	</div><div class="itemizedlist"><ul><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Controlled Access Protection Profile (CAPP)
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Labeled Security Protection Profile (LSPP)
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Rule Set Base Access Control (RSBAC)
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				National Industrial Security Program Operating Manual (NISPOM)
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Federal Information Security Management Act (FISMA)
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Payment Card Industry — Data Security Standard (PCI-DSS)
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Security Technical Implementation Guides (STIG)
			</div></li></ul></div><div class="para">
		Audit has also been:
	</div><div class="itemizedlist"><ul><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Evaluated by National Information Assurance Partnership (NIAP) and Best Security Industries (BSI).
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Certified to LSPP/CAPP/RSBAC/EAL4+ on Red Hat Enterprise Linux 5.
			</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
				Certified to Operating System Protection Profile / Evaluation Assurance Level 4+ (OSPP/EAL4+) on Red Hat Enterprise Linux 6.
			</div></li></ul></div><h3 id="bh-Use_Cases">Use Cases</h3><div class="variablelist"><dl class="variablelist"><dt><span class="term">Watching file access</span></dt><dd><div class="para">
					Audit can track whether a file or a directory has been accessed, modified, executed, or the file's attributes have been changed. This is useful, for example, to detect access to important files and have an Audit trail available in case one of these files is corrupted.
				</div></dd><dt><span class="term">Monitoring system calls</span></dt><dd><div class="para">
					Audit can be configured to generate a log entry every time a particular system call is used. This can be used, for example, to track changes to the system time by monitoring the <code class="systemitem">settimeofday</code>, <code class="systemitem">clock_adjtime</code>, and other time-related system calls.
				</div></dd><dt><span class="term">Recording commands run by a user</span></dt><dd><div class="para">
					Because Audit can track whether a file has been executed, a number of rules can be defined to record every execution of a particular command. For example, a rule can be defined for every executable in the <code class="filename">/bin</code> directory. The resulting log entries can then be searched by user ID to generate an audit trail of executed commands per user.
				</div></dd><dt><span class="term">Recording security events</span></dt><dd><div class="para">
					The <code class="systemitem">pam_faillock</code> authentication module is capable of recording failed login attempts. Audit can be set up to record failed login attempts as well, and provides additional information about the user who attempted to log in.
				</div></dd><dt><span class="term">Searching for events</span></dt><dd><div class="para">
					Audit provides the <span class="application"><strong>ausearch</strong></span> utility, which can be used to filter the log entries and provide a complete audit trail based on a number of conditions.
				</div></dd><dt><span class="term">Running summary reports</span></dt><dd><div class="para">
					The <span class="application"><strong>aureport</strong></span> utility can be used to generate, among other things, daily reports of recorded events. A system administrator can then analyze these reports and investigate suspicious activity furthermore.
				</div></dd><dt><span class="term">Monitoring network access</span></dt><dd><div class="para">
					The <span class="application"><strong>iptables</strong></span> and <span class="application"><strong>ebtables</strong></span> utilities can be configured to trigger Audit events, allowing system administrators to monitor network access.
				</div></dd></dl></div><div class="note"><div class="admonition_header" slot="header"><p><strong>Note</strong></p></div><rh-alert class="admonition" state="info"><div class="para">
			System performance may be affected depending on the amount of information that is collected by Audit.
		</div></rh-alert></div><div class="section" id="sec-audit_system_architecture"><div class="titlepage"><div><div><h2 class="title">7.1. Audit System Architecture</h2></div></div></div><div class="para">
			The Audit system consists of two main parts: the user-space applications and utilities, and the kernel-side system call processing. The kernel component receives system calls from user-space applications and filters them through one of the three filters: <span class="emphasis"><em>user</em></span>, <span class="emphasis"><em>task</em></span>, or <span class="emphasis"><em>exit</em></span>. Once a system call passes through one of these filters, it is sent through the <span class="emphasis"><em>exclude</em></span> filter, which, based on the Audit rule configuration, sends it to the Audit daemon for further processing. <a class="xref" href="chap-system_auditing#fig-audit_architecture">Figure 7.1, “Audit system architecture”</a> illustrates this process.
		</div><div class="figure" id="fig-audit_architecture"><div class="figure-contents"><div class="mediaobject"><img src="https://access.redhat.com/webassets/avalon/d/Red_Hat_Enterprise_Linux-6-Security_Guide-en-US/images/3ea2ab74ab03c7e846f1bc2a34f27967/audit_architecture.png" alt="Audit system architecture"></div></div><p class="title"><strong>Figure 7.1. Audit system architecture</strong></p></div><div class="para">
			The user-space Audit daemon collects the information from the kernel and creates log file entries in a log file. Other Audit user-space utilities interact with the Audit daemon, the kernel Audit component, or the Audit log files:
		</div><div class="itemizedlist"><ul><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
					<span class="application"><strong>audisp</strong></span> — the Audit dispatcher daemon interacts with the Audit daemon and sends events to other applications for further processing. The purpose of this daemon is to provide a plug-in mechanism so that real-time analytical programs can interact with Audit events.
				</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
					<span class="application"><strong>auditctl</strong></span> — the Audit control utility interacts with the kernel Audit component to control a number of settings and parameters of the event generation process.
				</div></li><li class="listitem"><div class="para">
					The remaining Audit utilities take the contents of the Audit log files as input and generate output based on user's requirements. For example, the <span class="application"><strong>aureport</strong></span> utility generates a report of all recorded events.
				</div></li></ul></div></div></div></body></section><nav class="pagination" aria-label="pagination" data-v-62e1e993 data-v-5facb650><rh-cta aria-disabled="false" class="previous-btn" class data-v-5facb650>Previous</a></rh-cta><rh-cta aria-disabled="false" class="next-btn" variant="brick" data-v-5facb650><a data-ssr="true">[["ShallowReactive",1],{"data":2,"state":2685,"once":2688,"_errors":2689,"serverRendered":16,"path":2691},["ShallowReactive",3],{"s8LoCEfG4A":4,"uUstF4AIyn":10,"Pn02PlJOas":2613},[5,6,7,8,9],"de-de","ja-jp","pt-br","es-es","en-us",{"name":11,"html":12,"type":-1,"toc":13,"breadcrumbs":1425,"error":19,"title":1436,"productName":1427,"pagination":2220,"redirect":2416,"canonicalLinks":2417},"Chapter 7. System Auditing","\u003Cbody>\u003Cdiv xml:lang=\"en-US\" class=\"chapter\" id=\"chap-system_auditing\" lang=\"en-US\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\tThe Linux Audit system provides a way to track security-relevant information on your system. Based on pre-configured rules, Audit generates log entries to record as much information about the events that are happening on your system as possible. This information is crucial for mission-critical environments to determine the violator of the security policy and the actions they performed. Audit does not provide additional security to your system; rather, it can be used to discover violations of security policies used on your system. These violations can further be prevented by additional security measures such as SELinux.\n\t\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\tThe following list summarizes some of the information that Audit is capable of recording in its log files:\n\t\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"itemizedlist\">\u003Cul>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tDate and time, type, and outcome of an event.\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tSensitivity labels of subjects and objects.\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tAssociation of an event with the identity of the user who triggered the event.\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tAll modifications to Audit configuration and attempts to access Audit log files.\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tAll uses of authentication mechanisms, such as SSH, Kerberos, and others.\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tChanges to any trusted database, such as \u003Ccode class=\"filename\">/etc/passwd\u003C/code>.\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tAttempts to import or export information into or from the system.\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tInclude or exclude events based on user identity, subject and object labels, and other attributes.\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003C/ul>\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\tThe use of the Audit system is also a requirement for a number of security-related certifications. Audit is designed to meet or exceed the requirements of the following certifications or compliance guides:\n\t\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"itemizedlist\">\u003Cul>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tControlled Access Protection Profile (CAPP)\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tLabeled Security Protection Profile (LSPP)\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tRule Set Base Access Control (RSBAC)\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tNational Industrial Security Program Operating Manual (NISPOM)\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tFederal Information Security Management Act (FISMA)\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tPayment Card Industry — Data Security Standard (PCI-DSS)\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tSecurity Technical Implementation Guides (STIG)\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003C/ul>\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\tAudit has also been:\n\t\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"itemizedlist\">\u003Cul>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tEvaluated by National Information Assurance Partnership (NIAP) and Best Security Industries (BSI).\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tCertified to LSPP/CAPP/RSBAC/EAL4+ on Red Hat Enterprise Linux 5.\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\tCertified to Operating System Protection Profile / Evaluation Assurance Level 4+ (OSPP/EAL4+) on Red Hat Enterprise Linux 6.\n\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003C/ul>\u003C/div>\u003Ch3 id=\"bh-Use_Cases\">Use Cases\u003C/h3>\u003Cdiv class=\"variablelist\">\u003Cdl class=\"variablelist\">\u003Cdt>\u003Cspan class=\"term\">Watching file access\u003C/span>\u003C/dt>\u003Cdd>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\t\tAudit can track whether a file or a directory has been accessed, modified, executed, or the file's attributes have been changed. This is useful, for example, to detect access to important files and have an Audit trail available in case one of these files is corrupted.\n\t\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/dd>\u003Cdt>\u003Cspan class=\"term\">Monitoring system calls\u003C/span>\u003C/dt>\u003Cdd>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\t\tAudit can be configured to generate a log entry every time a particular system call is used. This can be used, for example, to track changes to the system time by monitoring the \u003Ccode class=\"systemitem\">settimeofday\u003C/code>, \u003Ccode class=\"systemitem\">clock_adjtime\u003C/code>, and other time-related system calls.\n\t\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/dd>\u003Cdt>\u003Cspan class=\"term\">Recording commands run by a user\u003C/span>\u003C/dt>\u003Cdd>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\t\tBecause Audit can track whether a file has been executed, a number of rules can be defined to record every execution of a particular command. For example, a rule can be defined for every executable in the \u003Ccode class=\"filename\">/bin\u003C/code> directory. The resulting log entries can then be searched by user ID to generate an audit trail of executed commands per user.\n\t\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/dd>\u003Cdt>\u003Cspan class=\"term\">Recording security events\u003C/span>\u003C/dt>\u003Cdd>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\t\tThe \u003Ccode class=\"systemitem\">pam_faillock\u003C/code> authentication module is capable of recording failed login attempts. Audit can be set up to record failed login attempts as well, and provides additional information about the user who attempted to log in.\n\t\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/dd>\u003Cdt>\u003Cspan class=\"term\">Searching for events\u003C/span>\u003C/dt>\u003Cdd>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\t\tAudit provides the \u003Cspan class=\"application\">\u003Cstrong>ausearch\u003C/strong>\u003C/span> utility, which can be used to filter the log entries and provide a complete audit trail based on a number of conditions.\n\t\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/dd>\u003Cdt>\u003Cspan class=\"term\">Running summary reports\u003C/span>\u003C/dt>\u003Cdd>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\t\tThe \u003Cspan class=\"application\">\u003Cstrong>aureport\u003C/strong>\u003C/span> utility can be used to generate, among other things, daily reports of recorded events. A system administrator can then analyze these reports and investigate suspicious activity furthermore.\n\t\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/dd>\u003Cdt>\u003Cspan class=\"term\">Monitoring network access\u003C/span>\u003C/dt>\u003Cdd>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\t\tThe \u003Cspan class=\"application\">\u003Cstrong>iptables\u003C/strong>\u003C/span> and \u003Cspan class=\"application\">\u003Cstrong>ebtables\u003C/strong>\u003C/span> utilities can be configured to trigger Audit events, allowing system administrators to monitor network access.\n\t\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/dd>\u003C/dl>\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"note\">\u003Cdiv class=\"admonition_header\" slot=\"header\">\u003Cp>\u003Cstrong>Note\u003C/strong>\u003C/p>\u003C/div>\u003Crh-alert class=\"admonition\" state=\"info\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\tSystem performance may be affected depending on the amount of information that is collected by Audit.\n\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/rh-alert>\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"section\" id=\"sec-audit_system_architecture\">\u003Cdiv class=\"titlepage\">\u003Cdiv>\u003Cdiv>\u003Ch2 class=\"title\">7.1. Audit System Architecture\u003C/h2>\u003C/div>\u003C/div>\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\tThe Audit system consists of two main parts: the user-space applications and utilities, and the kernel-side system call processing. The kernel component receives system calls from user-space applications and filters them through one of the three filters: \u003Cspan class=\"emphasis\">\u003Cem>user\u003C/em>\u003C/span>, \u003Cspan class=\"emphasis\">\u003Cem>task\u003C/em>\u003C/span>, or \u003Cspan class=\"emphasis\">\u003Cem>exit\u003C/em>\u003C/span>. Once a system call passes through one of these filters, it is sent through the \u003Cspan class=\"emphasis\">\u003Cem>exclude\u003C/em>\u003C/span> filter, which, based on the Audit rule configuration, sends it to the Audit daemon for further processing. \u003Ca class=\"xref\" href=\"chap-system_auditing#fig-audit_architecture\">Figure 7.1, “Audit system architecture”\u003C/a> illustrates this process.\n\t\t\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"figure\" id=\"fig-audit_architecture\">\u003Cdiv class=\"figure-contents\">\u003Cdiv class=\"mediaobject\">\u003Cimg src=\"https://access.redhat.com/webassets/avalon/d/Red_Hat_Enterprise_Linux-6-Security_Guide-en-US/images/3ea2ab74ab03c7e846f1bc2a34f27967/audit_architecture.png\" alt=\"Audit system architecture\"/>\u003C/div>\u003C/div>\u003Cp class=\"title\">\u003Cstrong>Figure 7.1. Audit system architecture\u003C/strong>\u003C/p>\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\tThe user-space Audit daemon collects the information from the kernel and creates log file entries in a log file. Other Audit user-space utilities interact with the Audit daemon, the kernel Audit component, or the Audit log files:\n\t\t\u003C/div>\u003Cdiv class=\"itemizedlist\">\u003Cul>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\u003Cspan class=\"application\">\u003Cstrong>audisp\u003C/strong>\u003C/span> — the Audit dispatcher daemon interacts with the Audit daemon and sends events to other applications for further processing. The purpose of this daemon is to provide a plug-in mechanism so that real-time analytical programs can interact with Audit events.\n\t\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\u003Cspan class=\"application\">\u003Cstrong>auditctl\u003C/strong>\u003C/span> — the Audit control utility interacts with the kernel Audit component to control a number of settings and parameters of the event generation process.\n\t\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003Cli class=\"listitem\">\u003Cdiv class=\"para\">\n\t\t\t\t\tThe remaining Audit utilities take the contents of the Audit log files as input and generate output based on user's requirements. For example, the \u003Cspan class=\"application\">\u003Cstrong>aureport\u003C/strong>\u003C/span> utility generates a report of all recorded events.\n\t\t\t\t\u003C/div>\u003C/li>\u003C/ul>\u003C/div>\u003C/div>\u003C/div>\u003C/body>",[14,21,187,874,1023,1028,1043,1068,1137,1266,1296,1334,1339,1398,1413,1419],{"title":15,"visible":16,"weight":17,"urlFragment":18,"anchor":19,"singlePageAnchor":19,"url":20},"Security Guide",true,1,"index",null,"/documentation/red_hat_enterprise_linux/6/html/security_guide/index",{"title":22,"visible":16,"weight":23,"urlFragment":24,"anchor":19,"singlePageAnchor":25,"sections":26,"url":186},"1.
